<div id="review_1736744868" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1736744868" />

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Andre Gonzalez" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Andre Gonzalez" href="/user/show/53583787-andre-gonzalez">Andre Gonzalez</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1736744868" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1694660423638945863">I don't usually like non-fiction books from fiction authors, but if you're a fan of horror, this is a must read! Even with some of the material outdated, many of the topics that Stephen King discusses still remain relevant in the genre today. This book felt as if Stephen was sitting with you on the front porch and spilling his thoughts!</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_3380429481" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3380429481" />
    <a title="Travis" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7827751-travis"><img alt="Travis" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1575146978p2/7827751.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3380429481?book_show_action=true">Sep 12, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Travis" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Travis" href="/user/show/7827751-travis">Travis</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7827751-travis?shelf=reference">reference</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7827751-travis?shelf=horror">horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7827751-travis?shelf=non-fiction">non-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3380429481" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17009060764301795085">Fun but far from exhaustive survey of the horror genre circa 1981, with a specific focus on Things Stephen King Likes. <br/><br/>I dig King a lot and this is worth a spin if you do too, but the language often smacks of a young guy who's bitten off more than he can chew, vacillating between academic theory and a working class mistrust of the same. <br/><br/>A few factual errors in there, too, which was surprising; I didn't keep a running tally, it's just that every so often he'd toss off a verifiably wrong bit of in</span>
  <span id="freeText17009060764301795085" style="display:none">Fun but far from exhaustive survey of the horror genre circa 1981, with a specific focus on Things Stephen King Likes. <br /><br />I dig King a lot and this is worth a spin if you do too, but the language often smacks of a young guy who's bitten off more than he can chew, vacillating between academic theory and a working class mistrust of the same. <br /><br />A few factual errors in there, too, which was surprising; I didn't keep a running tally, it's just that every so often he'd toss off a verifiably wrong bit of info that made me frown. There's also the odd needlessly mean swipe at fellow genre writers that felt uncalled for - hoping William Peter Blatty never published again while elevating James Herbert is a pretty out there position to hold, but that's where he plants his flag.<br /><br />Which is fine, of course. At the time of writing (2020) we're in the middle of the Great Stephen King Renaissance and Danse Macabre serves best as a historical artifact from The First Age. It's interesting to see how horror and other genre works fit into the broader cultural landscape then compared to now, just as it's interesting to compare King's (and Harlan Ellison's) observations on TV from our current position in the age of streaming media and prestige television. Some of King's off the cuff jokes and cultural observations have not aged well, but that's to be expected, and he's a bit too hung up on his Appollonian/Dionysian binary, but you'll almost certainly come away from this one with a decent list of books and movies to hunt down, and that may very well have been the object of the exercise all along.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17009060764301795085" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3604932877" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3604932877" />

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3604932877?book_show_action=true">Oct 23, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nicole" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nicole" href="/user/show/54689236-nicole">Nicole</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3604932877" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer18040762755034501002">This is an interesting book but I did really struggle with it. <br/><br/>In a nutshell this book is part autobiographical and part discussion on the horror books, films and TV shows which inspired Stephen king. <br/><br/>While this book was fascinating and did give me some great recs to check out, I struggled because obviously this book was written in the 80s. So the horror he discusses is mainly from the 50s,60s and 70s. <br/><br/>I would love to see an up to date version discussion the modern horror books and films. I thin</span>
  <span id="freeText18040762755034501002" style="display:none">This is an interesting book but I did really struggle with it. <br /><br />In a nutshell this book is part autobiographical and part discussion on the horror books, films and TV shows which inspired Stephen king. <br /><br />While this book was fascinating and did give me some great recs to check out, I struggled because obviously this book was written in the 80s. So the horror he discusses is mainly from the 50s,60s and 70s. <br /><br />I would love to see an up to date version discussion the modern horror books and films. I think I might enjoy that more as I'll be more familiar with the content being discussed.<br /><br />If you not a die hard horror fan there is probably references and things mentioned in this book which will go over your head. I know I certainly struggled with a lot of the things he was referring to. <br /><br />I also found this book rambled on for a long time about things I didn't really care about. Obviously horror is a large genre so there is lots to discuss but I definitely felt this book could be more succinct in places. <br /><br />Overall, this was interesting and I did pick up some recommendations however, its never going to be my favourite Stephen king book nor one I'll probably return to and read all the way through again</span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1904334271" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1904334271" />
    <a title="Nick Iuppa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/22429985-nick-iuppa"><img alt="Nick Iuppa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442896406p2/22429985.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1904334271?book_show_action=true">Feb 05, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nick Iuppa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nick Iuppa" href="/user/show/22429985-nick-iuppa">Nick Iuppa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1904334271" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7577776473079075033">Before King became a successful writer, he supported himself as a teacher including a stint at the University of Mane. His book On Writing gives us a chance to understand what it would be like to have Mr. King teach composition. Dance Macabre gives us a pretty good understand of what one of his courses on the history of literature would be like, and, of course, this would be a course in the history of horror, Si-Fi, and fantasy literature and we’d have to expand our definition to include horror </span>
  <span id="freeText7577776473079075033" style="display:none">Before King became a successful writer, he supported himself as a teacher including a stint at the University of Mane. His book On Writing gives us a chance to understand what it would be like to have Mr. King teach composition. Dance Macabre gives us a pretty good understand of what one of his courses on the history of literature would be like, and, of course, this would be a course in the history of horror, Si-Fi, and fantasy literature and we’d have to expand our definition to include horror movies, comics, radio, and TV.<br /><br />The work is exhaustive providing extensive plot descriptions and quotes from King’s favorites including The Haunting of Hill House, Something Wicked This way Comes, The Shrinking Man, the Thriller TV series, The Night of The Living Dead, Psycho, Them, Tarantula and plenty of the other giant bug movies of the 50s. <br /><br />It’s all laid out with studied academic precisions, reason, and rules. (Horror is - at its core - a force for the status quo and is, therefore, a reinforcement of a conservative point of view. The things we are most afraid of are personified in three great novels of the 19th century: Dracula, Frankenstein, and Dr. Jekyll and Mr. Hyde. <br /><br />The tone of Danse Macabre is pure King: funny, sarcastic, and opinionated (Rod Serling wasn’t much of a writer and The Twilight Zone wasn’t really a horror series, or very good either.) <br /><br />As wonderful as that narrative tone is when you hear it in King’s own voice (like his audiobook version of On Writing), I wouldn’t recommend the audio version of Dance Macabre. The narrator/reader William Dufris really overplays the voices and the accents of characters and personalities alike, and he’s just a little too glib to give us the attitude we get when we hear Mr. King. The book is worth the read, though, and then you can buzz through some of those extra Bug movie scenarios and comic book plots that refer the titles that may still have been relevant in 1980 but are probably impossible to find today. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="7577776473079075033" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1663390-sherry-sethurner?shelf=nonfiction">nonfiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1663390-sherry-sethurner?shelf=sci-fi-fantasy-horror">sci-fi-fantasy-horror</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer36416226" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3525885301319777542">I was in a bookstore in Bangor, Maine looking at all the foreign editions of this book when a teenager mumbled that Danse Macabre is Stephen King's worst book. I beg to differ. This is a nonfiction analysis of the horror genre, both fiction and film, and it was really interesting to me. In fact, I photocopied the suggested reading in the back of the book and worked my way through the lists - it took about five years. I'm sure it's out of date, and that many of the titles he suggests are even har</span>
  <span id="freeText3525885301319777542" style="display:none">I was in a bookstore in Bangor, Maine looking at all the foreign editions of this book when a teenager mumbled that Danse Macabre is Stephen King's worst book. I beg to differ. This is a nonfiction analysis of the horror genre, both fiction and film, and it was really interesting to me. In fact, I photocopied the suggested reading in the back of the book and worked my way through the lists - it took about five years. I'm sure it's out of date, and that many of the titles he suggests are even harder to find now, but I still think the master knows horror. I'd love to see an updated edition.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3525885301319777542" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1256931112" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10496203352729914232">a really fun book even though it doesn't tell you anything new about horror. i mean unless you've never thought about horror at all. king is just such a great storyteller, it's all the side-tracks and footnotes and tossed-off stuff which makes the book so interesting.<br/><br/>also i need to read some davis grubb. gerald kersh. and james herbert.<br/><br/>and i really need to finally see dementia-13. why haven't i seen that. major failing<br/><br/></span>

          </span>
        </div>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('nH/sFLh0xx8gRtL60/kH4777UvRxGK+cHiu8jS0Kj4Mz7IbdRycR0SeA3gGyTZe9pgZpNCQYJoMUB4IadBdCiw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('7DYs7GodrU8xgqX3+TK/hGxzc8DD0gb16gU6Zv5gfnVDpUYllU57gTZEqQyYhi/adI5IAJbSj+rgKQTxp32zfQ==')})
  }
//]]>

Skal chronicles one of our most popular and pervasive modes of cultural expression. He explores the disguised form in which Hollywood\'s classic horror movies played out the traumas of two world wars and the Depression; the nightmare visions of invasion and mind control catalyzed by the Cold War; the preoccupation with demon children that took hold as thalidomide, birth control, and abortion changed the reproductive landscape; the vogue in visceral, transformative special effects that paralleled the development of the plastic surgery industry; the link between the AIDS epidemic and the current fascination with vampires; and much more.       <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/3389.Stephen_King">About Stephen King</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/3389.Stephen_King"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1362814142p3/3389.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/3389.Stephen_King">Stephen King
</a></div>
<div class='goodreadsAuthorBadge'></div>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer17991128064685793101">Stephen Edwin King was born the second son of Donald and Nellie Ruth Pillsbury King. After his father left them when Stephen was two, he and his older brother, David, were raised by his mother. Parts of his childhood were spent in Fort Wayne, Indiana, where his father's family was at the time, and in Stratford, Connecticut. When Stephen was eleven, his mother brought her children back to Durham, M</span>
  <span id="freeText17991128064685793101" style="display:none">Stephen Edwin King was born the second son of Donald and Nellie Ruth Pillsbury King. After his father left them when Stephen was two, he and his older brother, David, were raised by his mother. Parts of his childhood were spent in Fort Wayne, Indiana, where his father's family was at the time, and in Stratford, Connecticut. When Stephen was eleven, his mother brought her children back to Durham, Maine, for good. Her parents, Guy and Nellie Pillsbury, had become incapacitated with old age, and Ruth King was persuaded by her sisters to take over the physical care of them. Other family members provided a small house in Durham and financial support. After Stephen's grandparents passed away, Mrs. King found work in the kitchens of Pineland, a nearby residential facility for the mentally challenged.<br /><br />Stephen attended the grammar school in Durham and Lisbon Falls High School, graduating in 1966. From his sophomore year at the University of Maine at Orono, he wrote a weekly column for the school newspaper, THE MAINE CAMPUS. He was also active in student politics, serving as a member of the Student Senate. He came to support the anti-war movement on the Orono campus, arriving at his stance from a conservative view that the war in Vietnam was unconstitutional. He graduated in 1970, with a B.A. in English and qualified to teach on the high school level. A draft board examination immediately post-graduation found him 4-F on grounds of high blood pressure, limited vision, flat feet, and punctured eardrums.<br /><br />He met Tabitha Spruce in the stacks of the Fogler Library at the University, where they both worked as students; they married in January of 1971. As Stephen was unable to find placement as a teacher immediately, the Kings lived on his earnings as a laborer at an industrial laundry, and her student loan and savings, with an occasional boost from a short story sale to men's magazines.<br /><br />Stephen made his first professional short story sale ("The Glass Floor") to <i>Startling Mystery Stories</i> in 1967. Throughout the early years of his marriage, he continued to sell stories to men's magazines. Many were gathered into the <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10628.Night_Shift" title="Night Shift" rel="nofollow noopener">Night Shift</a> collection or appeared in other anthologies.<br /><br />In the fall of 1971, Stephen began teaching English at Hampden Academy, the public high school in Hampden, Maine. Writing in the evenings and on the weekends, he continued to produce short stories and to work on novels.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17991128064685793101" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
</div>
